<div id="review_1192902623" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1192902623" />
    <a title="Clarice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2287836-clarice"><img alt="Clarice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1416844021p2/2287836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1192902623?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Clarice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Clarice" href="/user/show/2287836-clarice">Clarice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11791890-revenge-of-the-witch">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1192902623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12824236926839982335">Although this is categorized as a Young Adult book and has a little blood and gore, to me it really seems tame enough to read with your 7+ year-olds, probably ok for 11+ year-olds to read on their own and might appeal to some adults as well.<br/><br/> The story is told in first person from the 12-year-old protagonist’s perspective. He is the 7th son of a 7th son, and, although he does have a “gift”, he is not a super-hero. He is a very likable and believable character. He is not supremely self-confident, </span>
  <span id="freeText12824236926839982335" style="display:none">Although this is categorized as a Young Adult book and has a little blood and gore, to me it really seems tame enough to read with your 7+ year-olds, probably ok for 11+ year-olds to read on their own and might appeal to some adults as well.<br /><br /> The story is told in first person from the 12-year-old protagonist’s perspective. He is the 7th son of a 7th son, and, although he does have a “gift”, he is not a super-hero. He is a very likable and believable character. He is not supremely self-confident, but he is very level-headed and thinks things through carefully before acting. Although, as a Spook (Ghost Hunter) his trials are supernatural, he does not get out of his predicaments with a magical wave of his wand. He has to use his intellect and tenacity – and, sometimes, a little help from his friends. <br /><br />Tom’s family is loving and mostly supportive, but apprehensive of Tom returning to the farm after he becomes a “Spook” because of their fear of what will “follow” him there. The antagonists are pretty much pure evil, but the niece of the titular witch is “neither good nor bad” and is unpredictable. <br /><br />As a bonus, there are lovely scratchboard illustrations by Patrick Arrasmith at the beginning of each chapter, and graphics of “The Journal of Thomas J. Ward” at the end of the book. Very nice touch. <br /><br />This is just the kind of book I would have sought out to help my young sons fill the void until the release of the next Harry Potter novel. After reading The Sorcerer’s Stone, they developed an insatiable appetite for fantasy literature dealing with young witches and wizards, and we were among the fans who would be waiting at the bookstore at midnight to purchase the latest book as soon as it was released. While waiting for the next HP, we would tear through all other similar fantasy literature available back then - T.A. Barron’s Lost Years of Merlin series and Jane Yolen’s Young Merlin series being among the most memorable. Although Tom is a ghost hunter rather than a wizard, this series would have been a most welcome addition to our reading list.<br /><br />I would definitely recommend this for young people and adults who enjoyed the Harry Potter series<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12824236926839982335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1699265925" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1699265925" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43590107-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460749949p2/43590107.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1699265925?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/43590107-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062120953" href="/book/show/13621780-revenge-of-the-witch">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43590107-ashley?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43590107-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43590107-ashley?shelf=meh">meh</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1699265925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2101438674875374257">Rating: 2/5<br/>***Minor spoilers***<br/><br/>Tom is the seventh son of a seventh son, and in this universe, that means he's special. He can sense things that nobody else can, which means he has the ability to become the Spook - the man who ensures that the supernatural bad guys stay away from the innocents. Tom is off to do an apprenticeship with Old Gregory, the current Spook, so that after all of his training he can take over to protect the villagers. However, Tom's training may have hit a bit of a speed bu</span>
  <span id="freeText2101438674875374257" style="display:none">Rating: 2/5<br />***Minor spoilers***<br /><br />Tom is the seventh son of a seventh son, and in this universe, that means he's special. He can sense things that nobody else can, which means he has the ability to become the Spook - the man who ensures that the supernatural bad guys stay away from the innocents. Tom is off to do an apprenticeship with Old Gregory, the current Spook, so that after all of his training he can take over to protect the villagers. However, Tom's training may have hit a bit of a speed bump when he meets a witch his age and learns of a plot that he has unintentionally gotten himself involved in.<br /><br />I didn't think this book was particularly good or bad, I just found it okay. I've read a bunch of reviews saying how this book was pretty scary. Personally I didn't find it that scary, but that's definitely better than the "horror" being cliche and overdone. There were some interesting elements thrown in that I found cool, like blood/bone magic as well as possession. <br /><br />I didn't think much about the characters. This was a pretty short book from what I could tell (I had an ebook copy without actual page numbers) so it wasn't a lot of time to add a lot of character development. I found Tom to be alright, and I think Gregory is definitely the most interesting character of them all. I thought Jack, Tom's oldest brother, was extremely rude without reason, and his mother is definitely hiding something that will be explored in another book in this series. Since the characters were nothing special really, it was the magical aspect that carried this book along.<br /><br />Overall, this book was decent, but I didn't find it that good. I wasn't bored, but I also wasn't too interested in what was to come. It was a bit predictable in parts, but I couldn't see any other way the book could go, which could've been a problem in itself. I don't think I'll go looking for the second book to read, but I wouldn't be opposed to reading it if I needed it for a challenge. There are definitely better books in this genre if you're looking to find one, but this book was by no means terrible, it just didn't stand out to me that much. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2101438674875374257" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('qqG7RuY0gZ7xVD1BwPPYbFLkOxGqhpWj03PJ8ztez7WQh9KUXWpI9lZ/iSA3BtKzhLvc2WQLG8SIDY9C9h09Lw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mAmdq+mOG+69aA7IyQJINJUQ+Gk98jQj0uxThSMDNG2iL/R5UtDShhpDuqk+90LrQ08fofN/ukSJkhU07kDG9w==')})
  }

Avenging the Owl deals with the difficult issues of suicide and depression, but more than anything it captures the powerlessness of being a kid.           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13443498574746578410">Joseph Delaney is a full time writer living in Lancashire, in the heart of Boggart territory.<br/>He is the author of Wardstone Chronicles, Starblade Chronicles, Arena 13, Aberrations and a new book came out in April 2020, Brother Wulf. This is a new spooks story featuring Tom and Alice, but introducing a new character, a young monk called Brother Wulf. <br/><br/>He first got the idea for the Spooks series when </span>
  <span id="freeText13443498574746578410" style="display:none">Joseph Delaney is a full time writer living in Lancashire, in the heart of Boggart territory.<br />He is the author of Wardstone Chronicles, Starblade Chronicles, Arena 13, Aberrations and a new book came out in April 2020, Brother Wulf. This is a new spooks story featuring Tom and Alice, but introducing a new character, a young monk called Brother Wulf. <br /><br />He first got the idea for the Spooks series when he moved to the village where he lives now and discovered there was a local boggart - ‘a man like me needs boggarts around’. He made a note in his notebook ‘a story about a man who hunts boggarts’ and years later when he had to come up with an idea at short notice developed this into ‘The Spook’s Apprentice’, the first book in the series.<br />He continues to draw upon the folklore of Lancashire and has acquired much local knowledge over the years which he tweaks and modifies to create his fictional world. Another source of inspiration has been Lancashire's varied and atmospheric landscape. Many of the locations in the County are based on actual places in Lancashire. <br />In the early days of his writing career Joseph worked as a teacher at a Sixth Form College: his subjects were English, Film and Media Studies. He used to get up early and write every morning before work. That way he could write a book a year – which promptly got rejected! When the Americans bought the series he decided to give up teaching and write full time. <br />Prior to teaching he worked as an engineer in his twenties, completing an apprenticeship just like Tom Ward in the spook’s books.<br />Joseph describes his method of writing as a process of discovery. He doesn’t plot too far ahead and often doesn’t know what is going to happen until he writes it down. In other words he makes it up as he goes along. He prefers writing dialogue to description, in which he says he is a minimalist and leaves much to the reader’s imagination. <br />Joseph has three children and nine grandchildren and is a wonderful public speaker available for conference, library and bookshop events.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2330711.The_Spook_s_Apprentice" title="The Spook's Apprentice" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Apprentice</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17426629.The_Spook_s_Curse" title="The Spook's Curse" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Curse</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17426189.The_Spook_s_Secret" title="The Spook's Secret" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Secret</a> have all been shortlisted for the Lancashire children's Book for the Year Award. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2330711.The_Spook_s_Apprentice" title="The Spook's Apprentice" rel="nofollow noopener">The Spook's Apprentice</a> is the winner of both the Sefton Book Award and the Hampshire Book Award.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.josephdelaneyauthor.com">www.josephdelaneyauthor.com</a><br /><br /><br /><i>from <a href="http://www.rbooks.co.uk/author.aspx?id=15205" rel="nofollow noopener">publisher's website</a></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="13443498574746578410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_15818358').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_15818358').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_15818358').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
